margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;</span><strong><span style=\"color: red;\">STAINLESS STEEL CHEMICAL TANKERS, &nbsp;SUS 316LN-&nbsp; CAPT AJIT VADAKAYIL<o:p></o:p></span></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-tVGfmbcL7Ys/T8QopCwIsoI/AAAAAAAALg0/9HBdlWdwNAM/s1600/imagesCA0O0WVC.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-tVGfmbcL7Ys/T8QopCwIsoI/AAAAAAAALg0/9HBdlWdwNAM/s1600/imagesCA0O0WVC.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p></o:p></span><br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The oldest example of\nstainless steel is antiquated as the iron pillar of Delhi erected 1600 years\nago by Indian king Chandra Gupta&nbsp;375 AD.. </span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-s44hNja2PgI/T8QmRzBxrrI/AAAAAAAALgE/sxi4PFHLdYc/s1600/sar_delhiironpillar.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"400\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-s44hNja2PgI/T8QmRzBxrrI/AAAAAAAALgE/sxi4PFHLdYc/s400/sar_delhiironpillar.jpg\" width=\"185\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Here the patina or protective layer oxide is\nnot by chromium but by Phosphorous. </span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/--_8MtD4Wffc/T8QmMCZDMiI/AAAAAAAALf8/V55wYRQAuT4/s1600/sar_ironpillar2.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"243\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/--_8MtD4Wffc/T8QmMCZDMiI/AAAAAAAALf8/V55wYRQAuT4/s320/sar_ironpillar2.jpg\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">However the presence of high chromium /\nnickel rock ore mines in India have ensured that some of the old steel weapons\nare still intact. Even modern technology has not developed any steel which is\ncompletely stain proof or corrosion proof.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Stainless steel is the\nbest for aggressive cargoes and acids..<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>Stainless steel corrodes in mineral acids, non oxidising acid solutions,\nreducing acids ( Sulphuric acid of &gt;80% strength is not very aggressive ,\nonly medium rage is aggressive due to non-oxidising character ), and hot\ncaustic whose corrosion rate increases with increased temp.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Chlorinated\nhydrocarbons also called halogenated hydrocarbons by themselves do not attack\nSS since they are non electrolytes. The dissolving effect they have on organic\npaint coatings is not possible on SS. It is the impurities which corrode. If\nthe decomposition products are acidic or contain high concentration<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>of chlorides rapid corrosion may occur.\nOxidation or hydrolysis (salt + water = acid + base ) reactions between\nChorinated HC and residual water can cause corrosion. The water content of\nChlorinated HC if greater than 100 ppm corrodes the tank. Oxidation is\nprevented by inhibitors. Obtain full specs incl impurities. This must include\nresidual water, Chloride and Hydrogen Chloride content. Clean tanks ASAP after discharging.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Remember Chlorine ( or inorganic chloride )\nin fresh water does not attack SS.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Chromium metal\ndissolves in Hydrochloric acid and dilute Sulphuric acid at room\ntemperature.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>But it does not dissolve in\nHNO3 because of a curious phenomenon known as passivation in which the metal\nbecomes covered with a thin unreactive coating. Ordinary iron gets passivated\nby Nitric acid due to the formation of Ferroso Ferric Oxide Fe3O4 film on the\nsurface of iron.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">On ships you do not\nallow crew to enter a SS tank without shoe covers. The idea is not about\npreventing of dirtying the tank. It is about damaging an armour and\ncontaminating it with the carbon of black sole safety shoes.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Stainless steel depends\nfor its corrosion resistance on the formation of a passive surface film, which\nis composed, mainly of chromium oxide. Although this film forms spontaneously\nwhen the metal is exposed to air or to water, it is possible to damage or\ncontaminate the surface during fabrication or during service so that the ability\nto form a satisfactory film is impaired. It is necessary to avoid or correct\nsuch damage if the optimum corrosion resistance of the stainless is to be\nobtained. It should be noted that the surface will usually repassivate if the\nfilm is damaged- if this were not so, the corrosion resistance of stainless\nsteel would be no better than that of a coated steel. Only when the chromium\ncontent of SS is<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>greater than 12% the\nchromium oxide layer (CrO2)forms.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The thickness of a well\nbuilt up oxide film is about one millionth mm on the surface of stainless steel.\nThe unit is Angstroms which is one divided by ten million of a millimeter.\nDespite the thinness of this armour provided, it will provide good corrosion\nresistance. A tank which has been hot washed for long must be allowed to rest\nbefore wall wash allowing the Chromium Oxide layer to build up. Since passive\nlayer consists of oxides the stainless steel has to be oxidised to maintain the\npositive layer. Remember the Chromium Oxide layer is invisible. The film can be\ndestroyed by active metals like iron particles or by oxygen starvation.</span></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-x3f-SBjqTGk/T8Qnit0PvPI/AAAAAAAALgs/JhpsjiWNksE/s1600/methanol+tank+2.JPG\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"240\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-x3f-SBjqTGk/T8Qnit0PvPI/AAAAAAAALgs/JhpsjiWNksE/s320/methanol+tank+2.JPG\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Passivation:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">A protective armor will\nform on Austenetic SS only if oxidising condition are present. Nitric acid is a\nstrongly oxidising liquid. Passivating with 14% cold Nitric acid is the best\nway to build up the chromium oxide layer with 2 hours of contact time. Then the\nSS has to be rinsed with fresh DI water till the pH is 7. This solution also\nacts as a thorough cleaning agent for stainless steel, rapidly and selectively dissolving\nfree surface iron while conditioning the surface for self passivation. (do not\nuse Nitric acid greater than 20 percent strength for passivation as the iron\ncontamination will not be removed).<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Conditioning possibly\ninvolves anodic oxidation of the surface.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>The nitrous gases which emanate while recirc in the tanks are toxic and\nhave a delayed effect.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Rinsing clean SS\nin oxygen rich water or storage in open air can also do the trick but it takes\ntoo long ( few days ) to develop to the correct thickness . Steel automatically\npassivates by the action of mother nature. So it is advisable to put 100 litres\nof fresh water inside a cleaned (to WWT or WW)<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>tank on the ballast passage. Air must be replenised regularly ( no\nforced ventilation is allowed ).<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Passivation with Nitric\nacid is usually done prior loading very aggressive chemicals. Passivation is\nnecessary after discharging even moderately aggressive cargoes like Palm fatty\nacids. Passive SS can be rendered active by dipping in Nitric acid heated to 75\ndeg c.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Hence the reason for cold nitric\nacid recirc. In circumstances favourable to passivity ss has a potential of\nnear noble metal. If passivity is destroyed SS is no different from<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>ordinary iron. Nitric acid &gt; 20% should\nnot be used for passivation as iron contamination will not be removed. In\nabsolute reality nitric acid removes surface contamination which would\ninterfere with the passive oxide film redeveloping.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Even ordinary iron can\nbe rendered passive by nitric acid due to the formation of Ferroso-ferric oxide\nlayer ( Fe3O4).<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Palladium chloride test\nfor active surfaces:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Passive steel does not\nliberate Hydrogen form Sulphuric acid. Palladium can absorb 900 times its own\nvolume of Hydrogen by Adsorbsion and Occlusion. Hydrogen gas reduces Palladium\nChloride PdCl2 easily to form black Palladium metal and Hydrogen Chloride.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">H2 + PdCl2 = Pd + 2 HCl<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">This is the reason that\nSulphuric acid or HCl<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>must be mixed with\npalladium chloride if the black precipitate of metal must be seen by the naked\neye. Passive SS does not liberate hydrogen. Palladium Chloride results can be\ntested using a mass spectrometer too.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Rinse PdCl2 with DI\nwater from a squirter as the black spot is active.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If free iron ( not\noxidised iron ) is present on the SS surface the iron is oxidised by Palladium\nChloride ( acid reagent solution ) to iron oxide.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">4PdCl2 + 4 H2O + 3 Fe =\n4 Pd + 8 HCl + Fe304<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Palladium chloride\ncomes in a small bottle with a dropper. The contact time should be 3 min\nminimum. The shelf life is one year if you keep it in the fridge in a coloured\nbottle. Unitor sells it. Palladium chloride crystals or deliquiscent powder is\nsoluble in water or alcohol.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Salt spray test</strong>:\npassivation is evalued by appearance of rust spots.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Copper sulphate test:</strong> a\ngalvanic type test in which the more noble copper plays upon less noble iron\nparticles but not on SS.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Patches of\ncopper sulphate shows a poorly passivated surface. Passivated parts are\nimmersed in a Copper Sulfate solution for five minutes, rinsed and visually\nexamined. Any copper (pink) color indicates the presence of free iron and the\ntest is considered unacceptable.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Ferroxyl test:</strong> causes\ncoloured iron compounds to appear as specks.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Passiprobe electric\ntest</strong>: a mildly corrosive acetate buffer absorbed in a porous test pad i brought\nin contact with the suspect active SS. The reference<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>passiprobe also contacts the porous medium\ncompleting the electrical current for measurement. Surface free iron will\ncause the passive reading value to go higher in the non noble direction.\nRemember free iron is not oxidised.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Rust in minute particles\ncan stay suspended in viscous heavy liquids like MEG which can fail a first\nfoot. Rust can accelerate polymerisation.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Passivation Oxyliser\nmeter test:</strong> </span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><em>The passivation meter sets up a temporary corrosion cell. The anode\nis the stainless steel surface and the cathode is the reference electrode. The\nelectrolyte is a suitable solution for the application and is applied drop wise\nto a piece of absorbent paper, which is then placed on the steel surface.<o:p></o:p></em></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The principle is based\non the electrochemical rest potential. This is one of the most direct ways to\nmeasure passivity. It is faster and more accurate than palladium chloride. The\nmillivolt scale is from 0 to 100, in passivity units.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">It is used to check the\npresence of free iron.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Measuring temperature\nis 15 to 25C<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The surface to be tested\nmust be free of rust , colours and stains.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Connect the black\nreference electrode and the red anode clamp to the oxiliser.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Remove the plastic\nsoaker bottle from the tip of the reference electrode and clean tip properly\nwith a tissue.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Connect the red clamp\nwith SS<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Moisten a filter paper\nstrip with the fluid for SS. The paper should be wetted properly. Place this\npaper on the SS.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Place the tip of the\nreference electrode on the paper.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The tip must make good\ncontact with the fluid.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Read off on the LCD\ndisplay\u2014wait 10 seconds for reading to stabilise.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">&lt;60 low passivity--\nand reducing<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">&gt;60 good\npassivity.\u2014and increasing<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Steady values upto 90\nare possible.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If after 30 seconds the\npassivity is reducing\u2014the passivity is not good.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If the surface contains\ntoo much free iron\u2014negative values can be measured.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If you grind a piece of\nSS with scotch brite, the surface will be activated and value &lt;30 which will\nslowly increase can be measured<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If you scratch the SS\nwith a iron nail&lt;10 and reducing can be measured.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The ref electrode\nshould be immersed in 3.8 molar potassium chloride solution.\u2014there is an\nenclosed soaker bottle filled with KCl for this.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Powered by 9V battery.<o:p></o:p></span></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Stainless steel is a\ngeneral name given to a whole family of high alloyed corrosion resistant steels\nin which chromium is the main alloying element. It is important that you know\nthe exact type of stainless steel 316L , 316LN etc you have inside your\nchemical tankers tanks for clad s/steel, solid s/steel ,steam coils , ladders ,\nsupports ,pump shell etc.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">It is widely accepted\nthat under oxidising conditions for steel with a chromium content of at least\n12%, an impervious and largely invisible oxide film forms on the surface which\nis self healing acts as a barrier between the metal and its environment and\nthis effectively reduces corrosion rate. In reducing conditions the film\nhowever breaks and the air formed film will not be repaired and corrosion will\nbe enhanced in damaged areas. Chromium improves hardness and wear resistance.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The inclusion of Nickel\nas alloying element improves the strength and corrosion resistance.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The addition of\nMolybednum up to 3.5 % will reduce the susceptibility to pitting attack, which\ncould result from the presence of chlorides. Molybdenum improves hardness and\nreduced enlargement of grain structure. On a parcel tanker it is important to\nnote which tanks have steam coils of higher molybdenum content for cargoes like\nheated caustic. Stress corrosion occurs in heating coils. Higher mo grades are\nmore resistant to pitting. Molebdenum is soluble in hot concentrations of\nnitric acid.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Stainless steel is\nclassified according to their crystal structure which is defined in terms of\ncomposition and heat treatment into following <strong>groups:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; line-height: 150%;\"><em><strong>Martensitic.<o:p></o:p></strong></em></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em><strong>\n\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; line-height: 150%;\">Ferritic.<o:p></o:p></span></strong></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<em><strong><span style=\"font-size: large;\">\n\n</span><span style=\"font-size: x-large;\"><span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><span style=\"color: red;\">Austenitic.<o:p></o:p></span></span></span></strong></em></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">When carbon distributes\nitself evenly in the iron the material is called austenite. It is named after\nSir WC Roberts Austen. The austentic stainless steel is generally used in the\nconstruction of chemical tankers, since they are compatible with a wide range\nof cargoes. The austentic grades have good workability and comparatively good\nweldability. Material formation of austenite group is like a cube. The boundary\nof the cube is corroded by any carbionic trouble., grain corrosion.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Austenitic stainless\nsteel is non magnetic and non heat treatable. The surface of SS is not so\nbright.</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ld1xBelknhc/T8cPGwkQ3WI/AAAAAAAALp8/pBnwH4t8DOQ/s1600/imagesCA7ZEL94.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ld1xBelknhc/T8cPGwkQ3WI/AAAAAAAALp8/pBnwH4t8DOQ/s1600/imagesCA7ZEL94.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ps6x7BdvIX8/T8cP1qIVERI/AAAAAAAALqE/qu1GCY_BCkI/s1600/imagesCAPG1NGM.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"228\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ps6x7BdvIX8/T8cP1qIVERI/AAAAAAAALqE/qu1GCY_BCkI/s320/imagesCAPG1NGM.jpg\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The Molybdenum free\ngrades are 304, 304L and 321 while the molybdneum containing grades are 316,\n316L, 316LN or 317 and 317L. The austenatic steel generally consists of C: 0.02\nto 0.10 %, Cr: 18 to 25%, Ni: 8 - 22 5, Mo: 0-4%.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>The notation \u201cn\u201d means it has more nickel for\nbetter resistance.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">304---Chromium/\n19%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Nickel/ 10%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Molybdenum/ nil<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>Carbon / 0.08%<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">316l--- Chromium /\n17.5%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Nickel / 13%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Molybdenum/ 2.7 %<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Carbon/ 0.03%<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">317l--- Ch/ 18.5%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Ni/ 14.5%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>Mo/ 3.5%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>C/ 0.03%<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">254smo---Ch/ 20%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Ni/ 18%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>Mo/ 6.5%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>C/ 0.02%<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Al-6XN--Ch/ 22%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Ni/ 25%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>Mo/ 7%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>C/ 0.03%<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The thermal expansion\nof stainless steel is higher<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>(1.8 times)\ncompared to mild steel while heat conductivity is lower (40%) and electrical\nresistivity is greater. There are great possibilities of distortion and warping\ndue to longer cooling time of SS. Therefore whenever possible clamps and jigs\nshould be used to keep the pieces in line until they have cooled.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Certain specific agents\nsuch as halides causes a local breakdown of the passive film on the steel\nsurface. This highly localised breakdown followed by electrochemical action\nresults in pitting which rapidly propagates into steel. Chlorides are\nparticularly conducive towards this form of attack even when present in minute\nquantity. Pitting hole is like a bulb and is difficult to detect without a dye\npenetrant.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Collection of solid\nsludges on the surface of stainless steel may also result in pitting. When\nsludge is known to be present in certain type of cargoes, means of circulating\nthe cargo should be provided e.g Phosphoric acid.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Crevice corrosion</strong>\noccurs with chemicals containing chlorides and other halogen ions. Rapid\ncorrosion will occur in narrow crevices / geometric irregularities in the metal\nsurface where oxygen cannot gain access. It is essential to design tanks with\nthis in mind. All welds are smooth finish and all spatter is removed. Different\nelectric potential can exist on metal surface with anode rapidly corroding and\nperforating.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Stress corrosion</strong> may be\ndefined as the fracture of a component by the conjoint action of a tensile\nstress in a corrosive environment. The failure of this is confined to\nenvironments containing either Sodium Hydroxide, Sulphides, Halides and mainly\nChlorides. Chlorides are particularly conducive to this form of attack and\ncracking, which is transgranular is found most frequently in the ph range of 3\nto 8. Cracking associated with caustic solutions may be either trans or granular\nand is usually confined to solutions of high conc and with temperatures in\nexcess of 60C. Causic embrittlement is the corrosion resulting in cracking of\nsteel stressed beyond its yield point due to localised concentrations of\nhydroxide ions breaking down the cohesion between the ferrite grains.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If the steel is heated\nin the temperature range of 500 to 850C the carbon may precipitates as Chromium\nCarbide at the grain boundaries. These areas become denuded of chromium and the\nprotective oxide film is prevented from forming. Steel in this condition is\ntermed as \"sensitised\" and on exposure to a corrosive environment will\nsuffer localised attack at the grain boundaries.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">During welding some\nregions in the parent metal near the weld will reach temperatures in the\nsensitised range, and subsequent exposure to a corrosive environment the steel\nwill be susceptible to this form of attack. This is also known as weld decay.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">This can be generally\navoided by using steel with carbon content below 0.03% max, and addition of\nelements with a stronger affinity for carbon than chromium like titanium or\nniobium.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Solid stainless steel:\nthe tanks are built of full stainless steel plates. Usually the corrugated\nforward and aft bulkheads are made of solid steel.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Clad steel</strong>: the term\nclad steel refers to a mild steel base plate to which a thinner layer ( 3mm )\nof a stainless steel is continuously and integrally bonded.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In this way cost of\nvessel could be reduced. The mild steel side is used in water ballast tanks and\nthe difficulties of bimettalic corrosion in connection with the use of solid\nstainless steel are avoided.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The clad steel is\nformed by:<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Roll cladding.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Explosive bonding.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Cutting:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Cold cutting: solid\nstainless steel plates are often cold sheared to size.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Hot cutting:<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Flame cutting with flux\nor iron powder injection<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Plasma arc cutting.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The oxy- acetylene\nflame cannot be used due to the formation of a highly refractory chromium oxide\nat the interface. But with fluxing agents injected into the cut the smothering\noxide is rapidly removed and fresh surfaces are continuously exposed.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Clad steel may be\nmechanically sheared to size, but this should be carried out with clad side\nuppermost so that any burr will be on the carbon steel side. When flame cutting\nit should be done from the carbon steel side.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Note: after gas cutting\nthe edges should machined or grinded to clean all scale prior welding. Plasma\narc can cut SS upto 10 cms thick with temperatures 11000 deg c to 28000 deg c.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Welding:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">A correct procedure and\ncorrect consumables should be used for welding of stainless steel to prevent\nweld joints to crack.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">It is important that\nthe heat input during welding is kept low to ensure a small heat affected zone\nand exposure to the sensitising temperature range for the shortest possible\ntime.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Spatter and rough\nsurfaces can result in local breakdown in passivity resulting in pitting.\nPrecautions should be taken before welding commences to prevent any spatter\nformed from adhering to the surface adjacent to the weld by employing masking\ntape or by applying suitable temporary coating.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The welds should be\nsmooth free from porosity, inclusions and cavities and carried by competent\nwelders.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Welding of solid\nstainless steels-<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">For butt welds the vee\npreparation has been used successfully in the construction of ships tanks for\nboth flat and vertical positions. Some times for welding of thick plates copper\nbacking bars are used. The copper backing bars extracts heat during welding and\nalso gives profile to the root bead.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In order to avoid\ndistortions for thicker plates double V preparation with separate runs\ndeposited alternately one on each side of the joint is used.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Welding of clad steel<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Welding of clad steel\nplates generally involves separate treatment procedures for steel base and\n\ncladding material. The weld deposit for the backing plate must at least match\nthe strength of the carbon steel parent material. The usual practice is to\nchoose an electrode, which would be used, if the cladding was not present. If\nthis carbon steel weld metal comes in contact with the corrosion resistant\ncladding, the weld material will be diluted by the alloy and the deposit is\nlikely to be hard and brittle.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">This problem is offset\nby using of filler materials having alloy contents greater than those of the\nparent stainless steel.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Generally the first\nweld made from carbon steel backing side should penetrate to the stainless\ncladding but not into this layer. The backing side should be completed before\nchipping back to clean metal on the clad side. Sufficient metal should be\nremoved to allow at least two runs of alloy weld metal to be deposited.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>The first two runs are made by using filler\nmaterials having alloy contents greater than those of the parent stainless\nsteel. For subsequent runs should be made with a view to ensuring that the\ndeposited metal matches the composition of the clad material and that the\nproperties are not impaired.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">For thin gauge material\nthe total plate thickness may be welded with electrodes comparable in\ncomposition with cladding material.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Generally all the\nfusion welding process like manual arc welding with covered electrodes, metal\ninert gas or tungsten inert gas welding technique could be used for welding\nstainless steel joints. Submerged arc welding is suitable for thickness greater\nthan 10 mm. The saw process gives high heat input hence it is essential that\nthe parent steel grade has a very low carbon content.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Light gauge electrodes\nand a low welding current should be used. With multipass welding the interpass\ntemperature should be less than 100C in order to reduce the possibility of\nprecipitation of grain boundary carbides.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Many of the processes\nused in tank construction affect the passivity of the surface. The metal\nsurface near welds oxidises during the welding operation and the oxide films\nproduced are less protective than the normal film.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The commonest types of\nsurface contamination which can lead to localised pitting in corrosive\nenvironments are:<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Embedding of matter\nsuch as iron and iron dust in to the surface. This causes pitting, pores in\nwelds and rough surfaces.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Entrapment of slag weld\nmetal.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Weld spatter</strong>- particles\nof slag and weld metal (from the welds in the tank itself or from structures\nadjacent to the tank adhering to the metal surface.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Coloured oxide films\nnear welds - these result in a dechromised surface beneath the film.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Splashes of paint etc\nwhich may stick to the surface with formation of crevices.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Care during\nfabrication:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Contamination of the\nsurface by iron, rust etc can be minimised by:<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Keeping the surface of\nstainless steel covered.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Placing sheets of\nhardboard over the ss when it is being shaped by rolling.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Coating surface with\nanti spatter before welding, which are readily removed after fabrication.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Stainless steel wire\nbrushes for deslaging etc should be used.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">A set of cutting tools\n/ hand grinders + wheels should be separately kept exclusively for stainless\nsteel work they should<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>be suitably\ncolour coded.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">As far as possible the\nhandling of carbon steel and stainless steel on the same work tables and in\nsame work shops<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>should be avoided. The\nstainless steel work place should be separately demarcated.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Do not put any carbon\nsteel / rusted equipment on the surface during fabrication.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The carbon steel tools\nto be avoided on the surface.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Men engaged on\nstainless steel work should not be permitted to use steel shot footwear.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">As far as possible\nhandling of stainless steel and carbon steel on the same working surfaces and\nin the same work areas<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>should be\navoided. Also prefabrication of stainless steel should be preferably take place\nin areas which are free from carbon<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>steel dust.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If grit blasting is\napplied then only clean sand or grit, uncontaminated by iron or rust should be\nused. On no account the stainless steel surface should be shot blasted.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Handling equipment such\nas slings, hooks and lift trucks forks should be protected with clean wood,\ncloth or plastic<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>buffers to reduce\ncontact with iron surfaces.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Final cleaning:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Although careful\nattention to the procedures described above will minimise surface\ncontamination, it is impossible to avoid this completely and some final surface\ntreatment, normally involving acid pickling and washing is necessary.this\nprocedure is often referred to as 'passivation' implying that some form of\nprotective, film is developed on the metal surface. In reality, however, this\ntreatment is to remove surface contamination which would interfere with the\npassive film normally developed on the stainless steels. Degrease tank before\npassivation or nitric acid will burn the grease into the SS surface.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>The pickling is done\nby:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Applying pickling\npaste. These pastes are based on Nitric acid or Nitric / Hydrofluoric acid\nmixtures and are applied to the areas of the tank where surface contamination\nis evident. E.g. Coloured oxide films near welds.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">To wash down the tank\nsurfaces with a mixture of Nitric acid (6 to 15 % by volume) and Hydrofluoric\nacid 1/2 - 1 1/2%<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>by volume) or somewhat\nstronger solution of nitric acid (10 - 20% by volume). Although Nitric/\nHydrofluoric acid is faster than<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;\n</span>Nitric acid care must be taken to ensure that it does not over etch the\nsteel surface. Another typical pickling paste<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;\n</span>combination is Nitric acid 14%, Hydroflouric acid 4.8% ,Ammonium\nBiFlouride 5%, tackiness increment agent 20% and other<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span>non ionic surface active stuff.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Remember Pickling and\nPassivation are as different as sugar and salt. Do not confuse one with the\nother. Picklings strips \u2013passivation armours. Pickling removed hard oxides\nformed by weld heat. It can be compared to the Johnsons liquid strippper and\npolish you apply in ships alleyways. Pickling involves metal removal and dulls\nthe visual brightness of SS. Sulphuric acid , phosphoric and hydrochloric acid\ncan be used for pickling\u2014which is removal of impurities.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Following is the\nprocedure generally used for<strong> final cleaning of tanks:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Remove weld slag by\nwire brushing / grinding. The uneven weld profile is ground smooth contour.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Remove weld\ndiscolouration with abrasive stainless steel wire wool, pickling paste or local\nswabbing with a pickling solution.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Wash the tank with a\nstrong detergent solution to remove grease, swarf, dust, paints, oil etc. The\napplication of heat to the tank will expedite this process.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Clean tank surface with\na 6 - 15 % nitric acid solution with or without hydrofluoric acid and continue\ncleaning until all visible scale is removed.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Remove as much acid\nfrom the tank as possible; wash down throughly with hot water containing a\ndetergent and empty.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If the above procedures\nare correctly carried out a clean iron free surface should be obtained on the\ntank.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">You can resuse pickling\nsolutions. If the pickling liquids iron content is &gt;5000 ppm renew the soln.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Over pickling must be\navoided. Uniform removal of scale with acid pickling depends on the acid used,\nacid concentration, solution temperature and contact time. Continuous exposure\nto pickling solutions for more than 30 mins is not recommended. The item should\nbe drained and rinsed after 30 mins and examined to check the effectiveness of\nthe treatment.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Acid cleaning is not\ngenerally effective for removal of oils, greases and waxes. The surface should\nbe cleaned to remove oils and greases before acid cleaning. After Sulphuric\nacid discharge brown discolouration is removed by pickling gel and then again\nrepassivating.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If any repairs or\nwelding have to be carried out on the tank after it has gone in to service than\nthe cleaning and passivation procedure should be repeated, although this need\nonly be over a local area.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Note: although the\ncorrosion resistance of stainless steel improves somewhat as the degree of\nsurface of finish improves, it is unlikely that any practical finishing\nprocess, for example hand grinding and disc polishing will result in a\nsignificant improvement over the performance of a hot rolled annealed and\npickled surface which has been properly cleaned after fabrication. The use of\nextensive grinding can result in significant loss of thickness, which may be of\nparticular significance in clad steel tanks. The value of grinding and polishing\napart from smoothing weld profiles and removing obvious surface defects, is\ndoubtful.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The fresh water is the\npreferred cleaning medium for stainless steel and where possible it should be\nalways be used.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Due to unlimited\navailability of seawater, it is often used for initial tank cleaning\noperations. Where this done a final tank wash with fresh water must be given to\navoid prolonged contact of pools of stagnant seawater with stainless steel\nsurfaces.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Piping systems require\nparticular attention to avoid leaving inadequately drained areas full of\nseawater it is not necessary to repeat the acid cleaning and passivation\nprocess unless the tank has been repaired or it has carried a particularly\ncorrosive cargo like phosphoric acid containing high levels of chloride and\nfluoride impurities. The acid could leave steel surface in an active condition\nwith pits containing corrosion products. In such circumstances Nitric acid\ntreatment after washing would be beneficial.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">For all practical\npurposes the general corrosion of austentic stainless steels in sea water can\nbe taken as zero. However the passive film on these steels is prone to local\nbreakdown when chloride ions are present. Hence pitting is likely to occur if\nstainless steels are left in prolonged contact with static sea water. The\nattack is likely to occur particularly at crevices or under deposits where\naccess of oxygen to the surface is restricted. Chlorides can locally attack the\npassive layer and prevent formation of new film. Stagnant salt water can\ninitiate pitting within 24 hrs\u2014you add some Sulphuric acid to it\u2014and time is\nnow reduced to 12 hours.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The addition of\nMolybednum to stainless steels improves their resistance to pitting and crevice\ncorrosion.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The possibility of\npitting of stainless steel is increased if the pH of the seawater is reduced\nfrom normal level of about 8. This can happen on chemical tankers which have\ncarried acid cargoes and cleaning of such tanks. Once tank cleaning is\ncommenced must continue without disruption to minimise contact between\nstainless steel and acidic sea water. The quantity of seawater used must be the\nmaximum possible so as to minimise the drop in ph.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Once sea water cleaning\nis started than under no circumstances the washing should stop till the tank is\ncleaned. The final rinsing after seawater should be carried out with fresh water.\nThere should be no possibility of leaving sea water for long periods static in\ncontact with stainless steel. The sea water temperature should not be kept\nhigher than 50C.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>It is important that\nthere are no stagnant salt water pockets in pipelines. There can be no pitting\nif salt water flow is greater than 1.2 mtrs/ sec.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Always clean SS tanks\nasap after discharge even if the same chemical has to be loaded again and\nagain.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In order to obtain the\noptimum corrosion resistance from stainless steel cargo tanks it is necessary\nto avoid damage to the tank surfaces. This can be achieved by care in design\nand fabrication and by treating the steel surface after fabrication in such a way\nto remove surface contamination.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Care in service should\naim at retaining the passive layer on the steel surface which will than provide\ncorrosion resistance throughout the life of the ship. Great care and right\nprocedure should be used for tank cleaning especially after discharging\ncorrosive cargoes like phosphoric acid and using sea water as initial cleaning\nmedium.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Chemicals which attack\nstainless :<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">There is a full lloyds\nlist available with this manual.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Some\ncorrode with impurities over the acceptable limit , some corrode due to\ntemperatures over the acceptable limit.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>A<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>few examples just for\nunderstanding are\u2014<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Benzene sulphonyl\nchloride<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Calcium hypochlorite<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Chlorinated paraffins<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Chlorobenzene ( benzyl\nchloride )<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Dichloro benzene<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Chlorohydrin<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Chlorotoluene<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Dischloroethane<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Dichlorohexane<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Dichloropropane<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Epichlorohydrin<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Drilling brines like\ncalcium bromide and cal chloride soln<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">EDC<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Formic acid<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Lignin sulphonic acid<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Magnesium chloride<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sodium salt solution (\nsodium hydrate )<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Perchloroethylene<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Potassium chloride\n(&gt;10%)<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Potassium hydroxide<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Propionic acid<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sodium chlorate<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sodium nitrite sodium\nsulphate<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Tetrachloro ethane<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Trichloroethane\ntrichloroethylene<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Urea<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Do not accept odd\ncommercial name cargoes unless you know the product. Many times such things are\ndone to beat the system for lesser customs duties, flouting Marpol laws<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>etc. Read cargo specs carefully. Add up the percentages\nto form 100% . If does not add up find out what is missing. Of if some\nimportant component corrosion accelerators like chloride or flourides are\nmissing from green/ black phosphoric specs find out why they are deliberately\nomitted.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Or if the moisture\ncontent of Epichlorohydrin is not mentioned find out why. For once the\nstainless steel has pitted you are responsible for destroying a good tank. Once\npitting starts you cannot carry sensitive cargoes like potable Ethanol or HMD.\nFollow proper sampling procedures. Keep samples safely. If tank gets severely\npitted get it analysed in an independent lab in order to challenge the false\nquality certificate.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>If the tank\ninspector challenges the condition of the SS cargo tank, counter challenge him\nby cleaning off part of the bulkhead where ever he wants with the product to be\nloaded to prove all is OK.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">If Hypochlorite\nsolutions are used for tank cleaning they must never be left in the slop tanks.\nBleach or Sodium Hypochlorite (11 -13%) is very aggressive to SS especially at\nelevated temperatures.they must never be allowed to dry up on bulkheads.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Kosher Acetic acid is\nusually loaded only in stainless steel tanks, though it pits and causes\nintergranular corrosion.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sludge sediment from\nPhosphoric acid made by the wet process<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>( Silica Quartz) accelerates corrosion. This is the reason why recirc is\ndone.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">You are not allowed to\nballast stainless steel cargo tanks without taking permission from the chemical operator. If it is necessary to<strong> ballast stainless steel tanks</strong>\u2014<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">1) Use clean water up to\n98% .<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">2) Raise pH value of\nballast from 8 to 11 using<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Caustic\nPotash..
