Say put 40 kg KOH flakes in 1000 tons sea water.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">3) Recirc<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">4) Short duration only.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">As soon as the ballast\nis out rinse with fresh water.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">After aggressive\ncargoes like Sulphuric acid preferably the initial quenching should be done\nwith fresh water. Sulphuric acid leaves liquid top surface profile ( wedge ) of\nexothermic corrosion. If it cannot be done immediately use nitrogen blanket.\nAfter dischg black/ green phosphoric prewash should preferably be with fresh\nwater. If sufficient fresh water is not available at least the first and last\nwash can be with FW, with the salt not being allowed to dry up. Acidic stagnant\nsea water is very dangerous for SS. Weld spatter areas are corrosion initiation\npoints. Weld spatter must always be removed by grinding and pickling. Remove\nweld discolouration by wire brushing and pickling with brushes.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Shipboard repairs:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Remember improper\nwelding of ss by pretenders results in complete loss of the corrosion resistant\nproperties. Do not burn ss while grinding. Use self sharpening grinding disc\nto avoid smearing. Ground area should be white and not blue/ brown. To prevent\noverheating the grinding disc must be constantly moved over a relatively large\narea ( use cooling air hose ) . The edges must blend in smooth without sharp\nedges and borders. If a rag is drawn and lint is shed the surface is too rough.\nWhen grinding remember the weld is harder than the ss plate. Always use\nmatching electrode for molybdenum , chromium etc. Use small dia electrode, low\nheat input and matching amperage. To dry pits use very slight preheat. Minor\npittings are ground. Use ss iron free zircon grinding disc of grain 80 ( coarse\n) or 120 ( fine ). Zircon has a hardness of more than 8 on the Moh\u2019s scale.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Major pittings are\ndrilled out like a valley ( the is to reach the bottom of the bulb ) and spot\nwelded and then ground smooth.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Never\ndrill out pits as a blow hole on a spot weld is a corrosion initiator which\nwill ooze black tatoo liquid once the non inert gas backed weld gets oxidised.\nPittings start at 1 mm depth and dia. At times they are hidden with tiny\nentrance holes to a big cavity. Dye penetrant tests are useful when you know\nwhere to look for pittings. If you do not know where to look for pittings you\nwill never find them. Small pittings are covered by a metal flap , but the\nsubsurface bulb cavity may be quite large . The clad steel is only 2mm to 3mm\nthick on chemical tankers. If the clad steel pitting has breached through ,\nfirst fill up with arc and then only with tig build up.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Any grinding must be\nfollowed by pickling and passivation. Cleaning before pickling must be done\nwith strong warm non caustic alkaline detergent. Pickling burns iron particles\nand millscale. Every 12 deg rise in temperature halves the pickling time. All\nrepair jobs such as welding, grinding etc., shall be pickled. Never pickle more\nthan 30 minutes. Over-etching of stainless steel may produces coarse\nsurfaces.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>Pickling contamination which\nwould interfere with the passive oxide film of stainless steel. Pickling\nreduces<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>pitting corrosion.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In welding SS with\noxyacetylene it is necessary to use a tip which is 2 sizes smaller than a\nnormal one used for mild steel. Since heat has a tendency to remain longer in\nthe weld zone of SS a smaller flame reduces the possibility of destroying the\nproperties of SS. A neutral flame is very essential for welding SS. Even a\nslightly oxidising flame oxidises the chrome in the SS thereby reducing its\ncorrosion resistant qualities. Since it is difficult to maintain an exact\nneutral flame it is better to use a slight excess of acetylene.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Specially treated\ncolumbium filler rods are essential for good welding of SS. If SS rods are not\navailable the second best way would be to cut strips from the mother metal and\nuse them as filler rods. Not only does the chromium in the SS oxidise easily ,\nbut the oxide formed during welding acts as an insulating barrier between the\nflame and the workpiece. Success in welding ss therefore depends hugely on\nkeeping heat to a minimum. Always use SS compatible flux and last but not the\nleast complete the weld in one pass. You do not weave the low current small dia\nrod weld in SS tanks. Strike the arc on an arc striking plate and then lead the\narc to the weld area. This is to make the welding current constant. Weld from\nedge to pit to other edge to avoid gas inside the pinhole bulb.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Welding rods for say\n316L must have a carbon content of &lt;0.03 and a Mo content of&gt; 2.4. If the\nwelding cable is too long, the voltage drop will be too great. If the cable is\ntoo small for the current it overheats and the power is lost.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">It is commonplace for\nageing parcel stainless steel chemical tankers to have on board a TIG welding\nset a MIG set and a plasma arc cutter. Of course every stainless steel shipyard\nwill have them.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>TIG </strong>stands for tungsten\ninert gas. The TIG electrode is non consumable. Inert gas prevents oxidation of\nelectrode. For joints where additional weld metal is needed a filler rod is\nused.</span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-lko8k5FKbR4/T8cMr3QabLI/AAAAAAAALos/gI-uajDv7_M/s1600/tig.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-lko8k5FKbR4/T8cMr3QabLI/AAAAAAAALos/gI-uajDv7_M/s1600/tig.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-MPcMlSy54-o/T8cMynugpWI/AAAAAAAALo0/iRLt18zQ6Q4/s1600/tig2.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-MPcMlSy54-o/T8cMynugpWI/AAAAAAAALo0/iRLt18zQ6Q4/s1600/tig2.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-s_2gKwxnBIs/T8cM4EYozSI/AAAAAAAALo8/-Ro3NJDvsx8/s1600/tig3.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-s_2gKwxnBIs/T8cM4EYozSI/AAAAAAAALo8/-Ro3NJDvsx8/s1600/tig3.jpg\" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">It is important to have\na weld that has the same properties as the base metal. Such a weld can only be\nmade if the molten puddle is completely protected from the atmosphere, to\nprevent oxygen and nitrogen from being absorbed into the molten pool ( makes\nweld<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>weak and porous ). No flux is\nrequired. Bonuses being very little smoke , fumes , sparks and weld spatter. If\nthe amperage is &gt; 200 the ceramic cup at torch head is water cooled\u2014otherwise\nit is air cooled. Argon inert gas is heavier than air and blankets weld well.\nDC weld has pointed electrode and AC weld has spherical electrode. DC weld\ncauses magnetised weld. In AC machine the electrode is not touched for starting\nthe arc, unlike DC machine. The filler rod physical properties must be similar\nto the base metal. On light guage metals backing is used to protect the\nunderside of the weld from atmospheric contamination. On heavier stock the\ncopper backup bars draw the excess heat.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>MIG </strong>stands for metallic\ninert gas. MIG set uses a continuous consumable wire electrode which is fed\nthrough the torch at preset controlled speeds. </span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-mrSzNrwA0y4/T8cM-9Gyg8I/AAAAAAAALpE/G8E3RNof7jQ/s1600/mig.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-mrSzNrwA0y4/T8cM-9Gyg8I/AAAAAAAALpE/G8E3RNof7jQ/s1600/mig.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-29Q0B0EeCvk/T8cNHfoRWOI/AAAAAAAALpM/Ft4nTxYQYzM/s1600/mig2.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-29Q0B0EeCvk/T8cNHfoRWOI/AAAAAAAALpM/Ft4nTxYQYzM/s1600/mig2.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-__8UqJq7J5w/T8cNN251NtI/AAAAAAAALpU/G-bsY0pylAg/s1600/mig3.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-__8UqJq7J5w/T8cNN251NtI/AAAAAAAALpU/G-bsY0pylAg/s1600/mig3.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Less time is required to train\nan operator ( a couple of hours, to know the transfer type<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>). All the welder has to do is to pull the\ntrigger and weld. As a rule weld failures are often due to the starting and\nstopping of welding\u2014since this includes slag, cold lapping and crater cracking.\nSpray transfer has constant spray of metal. In globular transfer the molten\nball at the tip of electrode tends to grow 3 times the dia of wire before\ndropping down . In short cut transfer each drop touches the weld puddle before\nbreaking away from the electrode wire. Electromagnetic force squeezes the drop\nfrom the wire. The short circuit is broken and the arc reignites. Shorting\noccurs 20 to 200 times per second. Shorting of arc pin points the effective\nheat. Intricate welds are thus possible. Argon, helium and Co2 gases are used\nfor arc shielding austenitic stainless steel.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Generally surface\nporosity is the direct result of atmospheric contamination. The chief cause of\ncrater defects is due to mindlessly removing the gun and shielding gas before\nthe puddle has solidified.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Plasma arc cutting:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Temperatures up to a\nmind boggling 28000 deg C is possible. Plasma cutting is used in ship yards for\nhigh speed cutting of SS. Plasma is often considered the fourth state of\nmatter. The other three being gas, liquid and solid. </span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-dbzVmfdyNU8/T8cNVJl6A7I/AAAAAAAALpc/YsOXd8GJ7MI/s1600/pc.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-dbzVmfdyNU8/T8cNVJl6A7I/AAAAAAAALpc/YsOXd8GJ7MI/s1600/pc.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-YNZWvErcXnQ/T8cNaAuusHI/AAAAAAAALpk/vKtxgwlPfnA/s1600/pc2.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-YNZWvErcXnQ/T8cNaAuusHI/AAAAAAAALpk/vKtxgwlPfnA/s1600/pc2.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Plasma results when a gas\nis heated to a high temp and changes into positive ions , neutral atoms and\nnegative electrons. When matter passes from one state to another latent heat is\ngenerated. Plasma torch supplies energy to a gas to change it to plasma. When\nplasma changes back to a gas heat is released. In a plasma arc torch the tip of\nthe electrode is located within the nozzle which has a very small orifice. The\ngas emerges in the form of a supersonic jet hotter than any flame. It melts any\nknown metal and its velocity blasts the molten metal through the kerf. When\ncutting SS best results are obtained with an Argon Hydrogen or Nitrogen\nHydrogen gas mixture. Cooling water is used.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Plasma welding:<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">A central core of\nextreme temp surrounded by a sheath of cool gas. The required heat for fusion\nis generated by an electric arc which has been intensified by the injection\nof<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>a gas into the arc stream. The\nsuperheated columnal arc is concentrated into a narrow stream. This when\ndirected on metal makes possible penetrative welds without filler rods or edge\npreparation. </span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-5_KWCUEzDaM/T8cOIxd5z1I/AAAAAAAALps/fpjZYZCThVw/s1600/pw.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-5_KWCUEzDaM/T8cOIxd5z1I/AAAAAAAALps/fpjZYZCThVw/s1600/pw.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-cLVan3-ZEVE/T8cOOLxbbhI/AAAAAAAALp0/5W4pYjXF7Rg/s1600/pw2.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-cLVan3-ZEVE/T8cOOLxbbhI/AAAAAAAALp0/5W4pYjXF7Rg/s1600/pw2.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">So what is the big deal between tig and plasma welding?<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>In plasma welding the arc column is\nconstricted for higher heat. The arc plasma actually becomes a jet of high\ndensity current. The arc gas upon striking the metal cuts or keyholes entirely\nthrough the piece producing a small hole which is carried along the weld\nseam.during this cutting action the melted metal in front of the arc flows\naround the arc column then is immediately drawn together behind the hole by\nsurface tension and reforms into a weld bead. A heavy duty DC rectifier is used\nas a source of power for plasma welding. Argon is used as plasma gas and helium\nas shielding gas ( argon too ).<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Bottom line: fresh\nwater rinsing of stainless steel tanks after tank cleaning with salt water must\nbe done by tank cleaning machine and not by hand hoses.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Some cargoes like\nPhosphoric acid and Sulphuric acid may form brown stains in the tanks and will\nnot go with Nitric acid passivation or Metal brite. Such discolouration may be\nleft as it is.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">REMEMBER--Once the ship\nhas been delivered , unless repairs have been done or contaminated with carbon\nsteel or rusted by a very corrosive cargo--pickling is not necessary.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Know the temp of all\nchemicals to be loaded before accepting them on board.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Salt water at &gt;75deg\nc for &gt; 2hrs washing affects the SS. So after heated Palm oil Fatty acids,\nthe SS layer gets affected.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">When inspecting a SS\ntank use a magnifying glass, a good digital camera, a ladder and a good torch\nand chalk and a mirror. For cargoes requiring inert gas\u2014inspect the space above\nthe cargo level.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Carriage of aggressive\nchemicals:--<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Chlorinated HC must be\nstabilised so that no decomposition can occur. Temp must be less than 35C.<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp; </span>the ppm of components must be less than<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Water/ 100 ppm<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Salt/ 15ppm<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Hcl/ 15 ppm<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">For sodium hypochlorite\nsolutions check the resistance tables for the carriage temp and the dilution\nstrength. It cannot be carried on 316L and the clad steel will get holed during\nthe voyage. 316LN, 317L and 317LN can handle the cargo<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Allyl chloride at 20C\npits 304L to 317L the same amount. 317LN is effected less.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Benzyl chloride and\nBenzene Sulphonyl Chloride at 20C pits 304L, 316L, 316LN, 317L, and 317LN\nalmost the same.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Caustic potash must be\ncarried less than 45 deg c and less than 50% dilution<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Nitric acid of &gt;90\nstrength cannot be carried. Lesser strengths<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>depend on carriage temp .<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Eg\u2014<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">70% to 90% --max 50 deg\nc<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">&lt;70 %--max 70 deg c<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sulfic acid\u2014<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Must be &gt;96% and\n&lt;35 deg c<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Sodium hydroxide\nsolution, borohydride/ sodium hydroxide<span style=\"mso-spacerun: yes;\">&nbsp;\n</span>solution and potassium hydroxide solution must be less than 70% and 80\ndeg C<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">N-butyraldehyde,\nN-valeraldehyde and iso-valeraldehyde must be carried under inert gas padding.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The heavy oxides on the\nheat affected zone formed by a new weld repair can be removed by hydrofluoric\nacid pickling.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Nitric acid can both\nremove free iron and oxidize (passivate) the SS surface. It will not remove\noxides.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Hydrogen peroxide can\noxidize the SS surface but it cannot remove free iron to create the chromium\nrich layer that then oxidizes very readily in air to form the passive layer.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Citric acid passivation\nsolutions can also get high chrome oxide ratios on the surface, and good\nresistance to corrosion .<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n</div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; Vishnu got upset and advised Shiva, Tripura must be destroyed. <br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-yJMDIwSJjDM/T7h_loUWuuI/AAAAAAAALRI/jfFdsLkXTKU/s1600/vfe.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-yJMDIwSJjDM/T7h_loUWuuI/AAAAAAAALRI/jfFdsLkXTKU/s1600/vfe.png\" /></a></div>\n<br />\nIt was NOT easy as the city could tranform into a flying saucer powered by mercury ion vortex technology and crystals. The three cities&nbsp;could be destroyed only by a single missile due to a special boon the kings of Tripura had secured from Lord Brahma by severe penance..<br />\n<br />\nVishnu gave Shiva the deadly Pashupatastra ( <em><span style=\"color: blue;\">a scalar wave interferometry missile by which world war 3 will be fought</span></em> ) arrow which could only be triggered by a mantra which resonated the Pineal gland of Shiva. The missile on a search and destroy mission ripped through all the 3 cities of Tripura ( Atlantis ) and reduced it to ashes in a split second. <br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; This tear grew into a rudraksha tree.<br />\n<br />\nAll Hindu sages wear a rudraksha&nbsp;garland of 108 beads. Rudraksha has a scalar field around it and hence increases the wearers aura and protects him from evil.<br />\n<br />\nIn Kerala before proceeding for the Sabarimala pilgrimage , (the largest on this planet with 55 million pilgrims in 2011), the pilgrim has to undergo a purification ritual for 41 days. During these 41 days he has to take a bath at dawn and wear the rudraksha bead garland. <br />\n<br />\nHe will NOT engage in any wordly pleasures till he gets back after the pilgrimage. This includes sex, non-vegetarian food and bad karmas.<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tc922UDvQWQ/T7h_F5wOv0I/AAAAAAAALQw/hpS7FH4-lac/s1600/BBB.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-tc922UDvQWQ/T7h_F5wOv0I/AAAAAAAALQw/hpS7FH4-lac/s1600/BBB.png\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: left;\">\nRudrakshas are graded as per the number of facets on it, and it could go up to 21. &nbsp;</div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: left;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-fkKdeJK-Qf8/T7h_aeQwdcI/AAAAAAAALRA/rhMwwOhwA3Q/s1600/untitled.png\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-fkKdeJK-Qf8/T7h_aeQwdcI/AAAAAAAALRA/rhMwwOhwA3Q/s200/untitled.png\" height=\"155\" width=\"200\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: left;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: left;\">\nThe 2 faced one I got for my wife has immense mystical powers , as is representative of the Shiva -Shakti unity combine-- the male -female form of Shiva-Parvati. It enlarges your aura and clears negativity spots. You can wear it only after a bath in the morning. Women must not wear it during their menstrual cycle. Rudraksha must not be worn while visiting a funeral or when visiting a new born. <br />\n<br />\nYou should remove your rudraksha when you engage in any impure activity , including sex , smoking , drinking alcohol , eating non-veg food , telling lies etc, or you will be harmed . You are now conscious of your own hour by hour karmas. <br />\n<br />\nOthers will judge you too, as a unscrupulous pretender.&nbsp; In India you can get abused and pasted in a bar, or a&nbsp;whorehouse,&nbsp;if you wear a rudraksha&nbsp;mala. margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><o:p>&nbsp;When you allow a liquid hammer to happen on your ship, you must remember that you wake up all sleeping watchkeepers. Rest hours is NOT meant for shore auditors , but for your own safety.&nbsp; In port if a liquid hammer breaks a pipeline, you may go offhire, and there are NO prizes.</o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">On parcel chemical\ntankers you deliberately introduce compressed air in the cargo pipeline systems\nduring the course of cargo work. It is important to understand the physics of\nliquid hammer.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Water hammer occurs as\nslugs of water are picked up at high speeds in a poorly designed steam main or\nin pipe coils or where there is a lift after a steam trap. When you heat cargo with high stern trim in cold weather , you will need to constantly drain the unlagged steam inlet line at the aftermost point.&nbsp;</span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">The danger on ageing\nships is going off hire or having cargo delays.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">As long as you remember\nto start heating very slowly using the small main inlet bypass, drain all water\nfrom the main inlet pipe, and keep the steam coils full of water ( not steam )\n, do not allow steam to return to engine room by controlling only the return\nvalve ( inlet to tank 100% open ) there will not be much scope for water\nhammer.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In some systems, the\nflow may be at 120 feet per second, which is about 82 m.p.h. As the slug of\ncondensate is carried along the steam line it reaches an obstruction, such as a\nbend or a valve, where it is suddenly stopped. The effect of this impact can be\nimagined.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">It is important to note\nthat the damaging effect of waterhammer is due to steam velocity, NOT steam\npressure. It can be as damaging in low pressure systems as it can in high. This\ncan actually produce a safety hazard, as a valve or a strainer can be blown out\nby the force of water hammer.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Water Hammer in\nCondensate Return Lines<o:p></o:p></strong></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">In most installations,\nwater hammer in condensate return lines is caused by steam pockets forming and\nimploding. Frequently, the cause is a rise in the discharge line from a trap or\na high pressure trap discharging into a low temperature wet return line ( steam\nwinches return expanded steam , that is why the dia of the return pipe is more\nthan inlet , unlike tank heating systems ) . A lift in the return line after\nthe trap will cause water hammer because the temperature of the condensate\nleaving the trap exceeds 100 C.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Water hammer in steam\nlines</strong> is normally caused by the accumulation of condensate. All equipment using\na modulating steam regulator on the steam supply must provide gravity\ncondensate drainage from the steam traps. Lifts in the return line must be\navoided. In a steam system, water hammer most often occurs when some of the\nsteam condenses into water in a horizontal section of the steam piping.\nSubsequently, steam picks up the water, forms a \"slug\" and hurls it\nat high velocity into a pipe elbow, creating a loud hammering noise ( which can\nbe heard by a nearby ship ) and greatly stressing thepipe. This condition is\nusually caused by a poor condensate drainage strategy.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Liquid for all\npractical purposes is not compressible, any energy that is applied to it is\ninstantly transmitted. This energy becomes dynamic in nature when a force such\nas quick closing valve or a pump applies velocity to the fluid.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Surge or water hammer</strong>,\nas it is commonly known is the result of a sudden change in liquid velocity.\nWater hammer usually occurs when a transfer system is quickly started, stopped\nor is forced to make a rapid change in direction. Any of these events can lead\nto catastrophic system component failure. Without question, the primary cause\nof water hammer is the quick closing valve, whether manual or automatic. A\nvalve closing in 1.5 sec. or less depending upon valve size and system\nconditions, causes an abrupt stoppage of flow. The pressure spike(acoustic\nwave)created at rapid valve closure can be high as five(5) times the system\nworking pressure. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Unrestricted, this\npressure spike or wave will rapidly accelerate to the speed of sound in liquid,\nwhich can exceed 4000 ft/sec.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Pressure surge is\ncaused by Kinetic energy of a fluid in motion when it is forced to stop or\nchange direction suddenly. It depends on the fluid compressibility where there\nare sudden changes in pressure. For example if a valve is closed suddenly at\nthe end of a pipeline system a water hammer wave propagates in the pipe. Moving\nwater in a pipe has kinetic energy proportional to the mass of the water in a\ngiven volume times the square of the velocity of the water.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Water hammer can cause\npipelines to break or even explodeif the pressure is high enough. On the other\nhand, when a valve in a pipe is closed, the water downstream of the valve will\nattempt to continue flowing, creating a vacuum that may cause the pipe to\ncollapse or implode. You must have seen shore cargo hoses often getting\nflattened this way at the end of dicharge. This problem can be particularly\nacute if the pipe is on a downhill slope depending on the ships trim.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\"><strong>Air in the pipes</strong> can be\nreally difficult to get rid of. The laws of physics keeps air at the highest\nlevel and liquids at the lowest . As the water moves in the pipes it breaks the\npockets of air up into tiny bubbles. Then the water flows past the bubbles,\nleaving the air still in the pipe. These tiny bubbles moving around, and\nexpanding and contracting, are that rapid vibrating sound you hear in Framo\nhydraulic systems. <o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Remember to get rid of\nair from the highest point. Of course the jockey pump does its job of\ncontinious removal of air\u2014but not from the highest point , which can sometimes\nbe on top of the crane.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-BE4LPFOAgvk/T7NvxYvrSqI/AAAAAAAALJ0/O6KqanNUxCM/s1600/VADAKAYIL3.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"283\" src=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-BE4LPFOAgvk/T7NvxYvrSqI/AAAAAAAALJ0/O6KqanNUxCM/s320/VADAKAYIL3.jpg\" width=\"320\" /></a></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">-------CAPT AJIT\nVADAKAYIL<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 10pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n</div>", "author": {"id": "14410812789424637654", "displayName": "Capt. His entire army would surround the camp and\nprevent Arjun from reaching it. The next day saw the fiercest fighting of the\nMahabharata war. Despite that just before sunset Arjun was within striking distance of\nDuryodhan's camp.</span><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-EmAEz2SDDi8/T7Khc9Bwx3I/AAAAAAAALEk/we_dC4Doc_s/s1600/imagesCAA26EPM.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"320\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-EmAEz2SDDi8/T7Khc9Bwx3I/AAAAAAAALEk/we_dC4Doc_s/s320/imagesCAA26EPM.jpg\" width=\"244\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 0pt;\">\n<span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">However Krishna\ntold Arjun that he would never make it to the enemy camp in time. There was now only\none way out. Krishna would use his Maya or divine powers to hide the sun from\nthe sky. Arjun should pretend to concede defeat. Jayadrata would not be able to\nresist witnessing the spectacle of Arjun's death. He would come out of hiding.\nArjun should not worry about the sun having set. He should kill Jayadrata there\nand then.</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%; margin: 0in 0in 0pt;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ER_0O69H92I/T7Kgq4C1GwI/AAAAAAAALDs/9_OV2Y5IgNk/s1600/imagesCA9GDVI2.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ER_0O69H92I/T7Kgq4C1GwI/AAAAAAAALDs/9_OV2Y5IgNk/s1600/imagesCA9GDVI2.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">This plan worked to perfection. No sooner had Jayadrata\ndied, &nbsp;Krishna again worked his Maya and the sun shone brightly, after the brief eclipse. Seeing the sky\ngo dark Jayadrata comes out to see Arjun die. The sun then starts shining again\nand it is then that Arjun shoots the fatal arrow from his Gandhiva bow. </span><br />\n<br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-XYXIu1tm1vI/T7KhVRNr95I/AAAAAAAALEc/KMcPav1_rlI/s1600/imagesCAK7AL1Y.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-XYXIu1tm1vI/T7KhVRNr95I/AAAAAAAALEc/KMcPav1_rlI/s1600/imagesCAK7AL1Y.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">He\nsevers his head and using several arrows in relays the severed head is\nprevented from touching the ground, and is deposited miles away into Jayadratha's father\nViddhakshatra's lap, while he was meditating in his ashram. </span><br />\n<div class=\"separator\" style=\"clear: both; text-align: center;\">\n<a href=\"http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-p9pYNwXYyp8/T7Kj5LideHI/AAAAAAAALFE/SqdB8oK-bZo/s1600/imagesCAI5N1DX.jpg\" imageanchor=\"1\" style=\"margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;\"><img border=\"0\" src=\"https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-p9pYNwXYyp8/T7Kj5LideHI/AAAAAAAALFE/SqdB8oK-bZo/s1600/imagesCAI5N1DX.jpg\" /></a></div>\n<br />\n<span lang=\"EN\" style=\"font-family: &quot;times new roman&quot; , &quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12pt; line-height: 150%;\">Jayadhrata's father\nhad a boon that who ever cuts of his son's head will die as soon as the head\ntouches the ground.</span><br />\n<br />\n<em><span style=\"color: blue;\">BELOW:-The jewel encrusted golden statue of Vishnu valued at greater than 100 million US dollars , was unearthed in one of the minor vaults of Sri Anantha Padmanabhaswamy temple in Kerala, last year&nbsp;. Unlike humans, it has the \u201csuperpower\u201d of regenerating its limbs, spinal cord, heart, and other organs..<br />\n<br />\nYoung frogs are known to regrow limbs, though they lose this ability when they change from tadpoles to adult frogs. On the other hand, the axolotl retains it throughout its entire life, making it unique among vertebrates<br />\n<br />\nHumans have also been known to regenerate the tips of the fingers, including the bone and skin. I once lost the tip of my left forefinger on the ship--it has regrown fully.<br />\n<br />\nBECAUSE OF CHEMICAL POLLUTION FOR TANNERIES, GANGES MACROPHAGES HAVE LOST THEIR ANCIENT POWERS OF REGENERATION..<br />\n<br />\nInjecting a drug to get rid of macrophages in an axolotl\u2019s limb before amputation leads to the accumulation of scar tissue instead of regrowth..<br />\n<br />\nThis scarring, which happens when a protein called collagen becomes disordered, is a normal part of wound healing in humans, but it is unusual in axolotls. This result suggests that macrophages are essential for regeneration<br />\n<br />\nAxolotls stay 'babies' for their whole lives. Axolotls are neotenic creatures meaning they achieve sexual maturity without losing any of their larval features<br />\n<br />\nIf an axolotl is given a shot of iodine, it will experience a rush of hormones that triggers the animal's growth processes, and it will \"grow up\" and resemble a mature tiger salamander, their closest relative.<br />\n<br />\nHowever, this is not the axolotl's natural state. \"Grown-up\" axolotls are typically listless and die about a year after the injection.<br />\n<br />\nAxolotls can regenerate pretty much any body part. A number of amphibians are capable of regenerating limbs, but axolotls take this habit up a notch by regenerating jaws, spinal cords, skin and even portions of their brain. Axolotls can also receive organ transplants and will not reject the new organ.<br />\n<br />\nAxolotls have a genome 10 times the size of the human genome..<br />\n<br />\n<span style=\"color: red;\">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B0GJOjfYn74</span><br />\n<br />\ncapt ajit vadakayil<br />\n..</div>\n<div class=\"comment-content\" id=\"bc_0_72MC\" style=\"margin-bottom: 8px; text-align: justify;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"comment-content\" id=\"bc_0_72MC\" style=\"margin-bottom: 8px; text-align: justify;\">\n<br />\n<br />\n<li class=\"comment\" id=\"bc_0_70B\" kind=\"b\" style=\"background-color: #eeeeee; margin: 0px 0px 16px; padding: 16px 0px 8px;\"><div class=\"comment-block\" id=\"c1061350286957344881\" style=\"margin-left: 48px; position: relative;\">\n<div class=\"comment-header\" id=\"bc_0_70M\" kind=\"m\" style=\"margin: 0px 0px 8px;\">\n<cite class=\"user\" style=\"font-style: normal; font-weight: bold;\"><a href=\"https://www.blogger.com/profile/17821568266464145690\" rel=\"nofollow\" style=\"color: #888888; text-decoration-line: none;\">CK</a></cite><span class=\"icon user\" style=\"font-weight: bold;\"></span><span class=\"datetime secondary-text\" style=\"margin-left: 6px;\"><a href=\"https://ajitvadakayil.blogspot.com/2018/08/comments-overflow-for-inoperative-load.html?showComment=1535398556183#c1061350286957344881\" rel=\"nofollow\" style=\"color: #888888; text-decoration-line: none;\">August 28, 2018 at 1:05 AM</a></span></div>\n<div class=\"comment-content\" id=\"bc_0_70MC\" style=\"margin-bottom: 8px;\">\nPranam Captain Ajit,<br />\nSir if water has memory, and Axolotls have such phenomenal regenerative superpowers, then the water had this imprinted within, making it \"holier\" in its power than the Ganga waters.<br />\nAlso, is it correct to assume Danavas were closer to Mayans and Aztecs than Vedics of the later period. taarif , tarafdaar) which run\nunderneath the frets and resonate in sympathy with the played strings.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">This is about the\nefforts of Orpheus to retrieve his wife, Eurydice, (who was killed by a serpent\non their wedding night ) from the underworld. Orpheus went down to Hades to\nclaim her, and played so sweetly with his lute that Pluto allowed Eurydice to\nreturn to the earth with Orpheus, but on condition that he did not look behind\nhim until he had reached the terrestrial regions. Orpheus, however, in his\nanxiety to see if she were following him, looked round, and Eurydice\ndisappeared from his sight, instantly and forever.&nbsp;</span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 150%;\"><br /></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">This LOOKING BACK story is\nmirrored from the lore of Adi Shankaracharya bringing Devi to Kerala in 2000 BC\n\u2014&nbsp; he looked back and Devi disappeared at\nthe spot of Mookambika temple at Kollur Karnataka.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<br /></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Pythagoras learnt\nmetempsychosis from India.&nbsp;\nMetempsychosis is the Greek equivalent of the 11000 year old Vedic Hindu\ndoctrine of transmigration of the soul, Karma and and reincarnation after death.<o:p></o:p></span></div>\n<div class=\"MsoNormal\" style=\"line-height: 150%;\">\n<span style=\"font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;,&quot;serif&quot;; font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 150%;\">Almost every Greek text\ntells that Orpheos was famous for Ahimsa or non-violence .
